          <a href="/wiki/File:Beirut_Souks.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Beirut_Souks" title="Beirut Souks">Beirut Souks</a> shopping mall
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Lebanon has a very high level of public debt and large external financing needs.<sup id="cite_ref-expus_201-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-expus-201">[195]</a></sup> The 2010 public debt exceeded 150.7% of GDP, ranking fourth highest in the world as a percentage of GDP, though down from 154.8% in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_15-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-15">[11]</a></sup> At the end 2008, finance minister <a href="/wiki/Mohamad_Chatah" title="Mohamad Chatah">Mohamad Chatah</a> stated that the debt was going to reach $47&nbsp;billion in that year and would increase to $49&nbsp;billion if privatization of two telecoms companies did not occur.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">[198]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Daily_Star_(Lebanon)" class="mw-redirect" title="Daily Star (Lebanon)">Daily Star</a> wrote that exorbitant debt levels have "slowed down the economy and reduced the government's spending on essential development projects".<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">[199]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The urban population in Lebanon is noted for its commercial enterprise.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">[200]</a></sup> Emigration has yielded Lebanese "commercial networks" throughout the world.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">[201]</a></sup> Remittances from Lebanese abroad total $8.2&nbsp;billion<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">[202]</a></sup> and account for one-fifth of the country's economy.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">[203]</a></sup> Lebanon has the largest proportion of skilled labor among Arab States.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">[204]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Investment_Development_Authority_of_Lebanon" title="Investment Development Authority of Lebanon">Investment Development Authority of Lebanon</a> was established with the aim of promoting investment in Lebanon. In 2001, Investment Law No.360<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">[205]</a></sup> was enacted to reinforce the organisation's mission. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Agriculture_in_Lebanon" title="Agriculture in Lebanon">agricultural sector</a> employs 12% of the total <a href="/wiki/Workforce" title="Workforce">workforce</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-workforce_212-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-workforce-212">[206]</a></sup> Agriculture contributed to 5.9% of the country's GDP in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">[207]</a></sup> Lebanon's proportion of cultivable land is the highest in the Arab world,<sup id="cite_ref-agriculture_214-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-agriculture-214">[208]</a></sup> Major produce includes apples, peaches, oranges, and lemons.<sup id="cite_ref-dos-2010-03-22_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dos-2010-03-22-21">[16]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Commodity_market" title="Commodity market">commodities market</a> in Lebanon includes substantial <a href="/wiki/Gold_coin" title="Gold coin">gold coin</a> production, however according to <a href="/wiki/International_Air_Transport_Association" title="International Air Transport Association">International Air Transport Association</a> <b>(IATA)</b> standards, they must be declared upon exportation to any foreign country.<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">[209]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">Oil</a> has recently been discovered inland and in the seabed between Lebanon, Cyprus, Israel and Egypt and talks are underway between <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Cyprus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a> to reach an agreement regarding the exploration of these resources. The seabed separating Lebanon and Cyprus is believed to hold significant quantities of crude oil and natural gas.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">[210]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Industry in Lebanon is mainly limited to small businesses that reassemble and package imported parts. In 2004, industry ranked second in workforce, with 26% of the Lebanese working population,<sup id="cite_ref-workforce_212-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-workforce-212">[206]</a></sup> and second in GDP contribution, with 21% of Lebanon's GDP.<sup id="cite_ref-dos-2010-03-22_21-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dos-2010-03-22-21">[16]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Nearly 65% of the Lebanese workforce attain employment in the services sector.<sup id="cite_ref-workforce_212-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-workforce-212">[206]</a></sup> The GDP contribution, accordingly, amounts to roughly 67.3% of the annual Lebanese GDP.<sup id="cite_ref-dos-2010-03-22_21-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dos-2010-03-22-21">[16]</a></sup> However, dependence on the tourism and banking sectors leaves the economy vulnerable to political instability.<sup id="cite_ref-Canada_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canada-24">[19]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Lebanese banks are high on liquidity and reputed for their security.<sup id="cite_ref-Lebanon_Banks_immune_217-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lebanon_Banks_immune-217">[211]</a></sup> Lebanon was one of the only seven countries in the world in which the value of the stock markets increased in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-Lebanon_2008_profit_218-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lebanon_2008_profit-218">[212]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 10 May 2013 the Lebanese minister of energy and water clarified that seismic images of the Lebanese's sea bed are undergoing detailed explanation of their contents and that up till now, approximately 10% have been covered. Preliminary inspection of the results showed, with more than 50% probability, that 10% of Lebanon's exclusive economic zone contained up to 660 million barrels of oil and up to 30×10<sup>12</sup> cu ft of gas.<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">[213]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Syrian crisis has significantly affected Lebanese economic and financial situation. The demographic pressure imposed by the Syrian refugees now living in Lebanon has led to competition in the labour market. As a direct consequence unemployment has doubled in three years, reaching 20% in 2014. A loss of 14% of wages regarding the salary of less-skilled workers has also been registered. The financial constraints were also felt: the poverty rate increased with 170,000 Lebanese falling under the poverty threshold. In the period between 2012 and 2014, the public spending increased by $1 billion and losses amounted to $7.5 billion. Expenditures related only to the Syrian refugees were estimated by the Central Bank of Lebanon as $4.5 billion every year.<sup id="cite_ref-chronicle.fanack.com_220-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chronicle.fanack.com-220">[214]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="History_2">History</span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Lebanese_real_GDP_Growth_in_%25.PNG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Lebanese_real_GDP_Growth_in_%25.PNG/220px-Lebanese_real_GDP_Growth_in_%25.PNG" decoding="async" width="220" height="170" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Lebanese_real_GDP_Growth_in_%25.PNG/330px-Lebanese_real_GDP_Growth_in_%25.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Lebanese_real_GDP_Growth_in_%25.PNG/440px-Lebanese_real_GDP_Growth_in_%25.PNG 2x" data-file-width="790" data-file-height="609"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Lebanese_real_GDP_Growth_in_%25.PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Lebanese real GDP growth
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Frances_Guy,_Beirut_Dock%27s_you_can_just_about_see_the_snow-capped_peaks_(2213410431).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Frances_Guy%2C_Beirut_Dock%27s_you_can_just_about_see_the_snow-capped_peaks_%282213410431%29.jpg/220px-Frances_Guy%2C_Beirut_Dock%27s_you_can_just_about_see_the_snow-capped_peaks_%282213410431%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Frances_Guy%2C_Beirut_Dock%27s_you_can_just_about_see_the_snow-capped_peaks_%282213410431%29.jpg/330px-Frances_Guy%2C_Beirut_Dock%27s_you_can_just_about_see_the_snow-capped_peaks_%282213410431%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Frances_Guy%2C_Beirut_Dock%27s_you_can_just_about_see_the_snow-capped_peaks_%282213410431%29.jpg/440px-Frances_Guy%2C_Beirut_Dock%27s_you_can_just_about_see_the_snow-capped_peaks_%282213410431%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Frances_Guy,_Beirut_Dock%27s_you_can_just_about_see_the_snow-capped_peaks_(2213410431).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Port of Beirut
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In the 1950s, GDP growth was the second highest in the world. Despite not having oil reserves, Lebanon, as the banking center of the Middle East and one of the trading centers, had a high national income.<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">[215]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The 1975–1990 civil war heavily damaged Lebanon's economic infrastructure,<sup id="cite_ref-Stinson_192-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stinson-192">[186]</a></sup> cut national output by half, and all but ended Lebanon's position as a West Asian <a href="/wiki/Entrep%C3%B4t" title="Entrepôt">entrepôt</a> and banking hub.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_15-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-15">[11]</a></sup> The subsequent period of relative peace enabled the central government to restore control in <a href="/wiki/Beirut" title="Beirut">Beirut</a>, begin collecting taxes, and regain access to key port and government facilities. Economic recovery has been helped by a financially sound banking system and resilient small- and medium-scale manufacturers, with family remittances, banking services, manufactured and farm exports, and international aid as the main sources of foreign exchange.<sup id="cite_ref-cia2001_222-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia2001-222">[216]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Until July 2006, Lebanon enjoyed considerable stability, Beirut's reconstruction was almost complete,<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">[217]</a></sup> and increasing numbers of tourists poured into the nation's resorts.<sup id="cite_ref-tourism_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tourism-23">[18]</a></sup> The economy witnessed growth, with bank assets reaching over 75&nbsp;billion US dollars,<sup id="cite_ref-economy-stat_224-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-economy-stat-224">[218]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Market_capitalization" title="Market capitalization">Market capitalization</a> was also at an all-time high, estimated at $10.9&nbsp;billion at the end of the second quarter of 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-economy-stat_224-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-economy-stat-224">[218]</a></sup> The month-long <a href="/wiki/2006_Lebanon_War" title="2006 Lebanon War">2006 war</a> severely damaged Lebanon's fragile economy, especially the tourism sector. According to a preliminary report published by the Lebanese <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Finance_(Lebanon)" title="Ministry of Finance (Lebanon)">Ministry of Finance</a> on 30 August 2006, a major economic decline was expected as a result of the fighting.<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">[219]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Over the course of 2008 Lebanon rebuilt its infrastructure mainly in the real estate and tourism sectors, resulting in a comparatively robust post war economy. Major contributors to the reconstruction of Lebanon include <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a> (with US$1.5&nbsp;billion pledged),<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">[220]</a></sup> the European Union (with about $1&nbsp;billion)<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">[221]</a></sup> and a few other Persian Gulf countries with contributions of up to $800&nbsp;million.<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">[222]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Lebanon" title="Tourism in Lebanon">Tourism in Lebanon</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Beirut_002.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Beirut_002.jpg/220px-Beirut_002.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Beirut_002.jpg/330px-Beirut_002.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Beirut_002.jpg/440px-Beirut_002.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Beirut_002.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Beirut" title="Beirut">Beirut</a> is the tourism hub of the country
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Anjar-109900.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Anjar-109900.jpg/220px-Anjar-109900.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Anjar-109900.jpg/330px-Anjar-109900.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Anjar-109900.jpg/440px-Anjar-109900.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Anjar-109900.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Arches at the ruins of Anjar
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The tourism industry accounts for about 10% of <a href="/wiki/GDP" class="mw-redirect" title="GDP">GDP</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-lebtourecon_229-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lebtourecon-229">[223]</a></sup> Lebanon attracted around 1,333,000 tourists in 2008, thus placing it as 79th out of 191 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">[224]</a></sup> In 2009, <i>The New York Times</i> ranked Beirut the No.&nbsp;1 travel destination worldwide due to its nightlife and hospitality.<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">[225]</a></sup> In January 2010, the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Tourism_(Lebanon)" title="Ministry of Tourism (Lebanon)">Ministry of Tourism</a> announced that 1,851,081 tourists had visited Lebanon in 2009, a 39% increase from 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-lebanon-tourism1_232-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lebanon-tourism1-232">[226]</a></sup> In 2009, Lebanon hosted the largest number of tourists to date, eclipsing the previous record set before the <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_Civil_War" title="Lebanese Civil War">Lebanese Civil War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ABC_2009_Tourism_Record_233-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ABC_2009_Tourism_Record-233">[227]</a></sup> Tourist arrivals reached two million in 2010, but fell by 37% for the first 10 months of 2012, a decline caused by the war in neighbouring Syria.<sup id="cite_ref-lebtourecon_229-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lebtourecon-229">[223]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a>, Jordan, and Japan are the three most popular origin countries of foreign tourists to Lebanon.<sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">[228]</a></sup> The recent influx of Japanese tourists has caused the recent rise in popularity of <a href="/wiki/Japanese_cuisine" title="Japanese cuisine">Japanese cuisine</a> in Lebanon.<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">[229]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Lebanon" title="Education in Lebanon">Education in Lebanon</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Beirut_Universitet_Haigazian.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Beirut_Universitet_Haigazian.jpg/220px-Beirut_Universitet_Haigazian.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Beirut_Universitet_Haigazian.jpg/330px-Beirut_Universitet_Haigazian.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Beirut_Universitet_Haigazian.jpg/440px-Beirut_Universitet_Haigazian.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Beirut_Universitet_Haigazian.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Haigazian_University" title="Haigazian University">Haigazian University</a> in Beirut.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:American_University_of_Beirut_(4694793112).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/American_University_of_Beirut_%284694793112%29.jpg/220px-American_University_of_Beirut_%284694793112%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="178" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/American_University_of_Beirut_%284694793112%29.jpg/330px-American_University_of_Beirut_%284694793112%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/American_University_of_Beirut_%284694793112%29.jpg/440px-American_University_of_Beirut_%284694793112%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4103" data-file-height="3312"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:American_University_of_Beirut_(4694793112).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/American_University_of_Beirut" title="American University of Beirut">AUB</a> College Hall in Beirut.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Listed by the World Economic Forum's 2013 Global Information Technology Report, Lebanon has been ranked globally as the fourth best country for math and science education, and as the tenth best overall for quality of education. In quality of management schools, the country was ranked 13th worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">[230]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The United Nations assigned Lebanon an education index of 0.871 in 2008. The index, which is determined by the adult literacy rate and the combined primary, secondary, and tertiary gross enrollment ratio, ranked the country 88th out of the 177 countries participating.<sup id="cite_ref-undp_237-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-undp-237">[231]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>All Lebanese schools are required to follow a prescribed curriculum designed by the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Education_and_Higher_Education_(Lebanon)" title="Ministry of Education and Higher Education (Lebanon)">Ministry of Education</a>. Some of the 1400 private schools offer <a href="/wiki/IB_program" class="mw-redirect" title="IB program">IB programs</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238">[232]</a></sup> and may also add more courses to their curriculum with approval from the Ministry of Education. The first eight years of education are, by law, compulsory.<sup id="cite_ref-dos-2010-03-22_21-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dos-2010-03-22-21">[16]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Lebanon has forty-one nationally accredited universities, several of which are internationally recognized.<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">[233]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-240" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240">[234]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/American_University_of_Beirut" title="American University of Beirut">American University of Beirut</a> (AUB) and the <a href="/wiki/Universit%C3%A9_Saint-Joseph" class="mw-redirect" title="Université Saint-Joseph">Université Saint-Joseph</a> (USJ) were the first Anglophone and the first Francophone universities to open in Lebanon, respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">[235]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242">[236]</a></sup> Universities in Lebanon, both public and private, largely operate in French or English.<sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243">[237]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The top-ranking universities in the country are the <a href="/wiki/American_University_of_Beirut" title="American University of Beirut">American University of Beirut</a> (#220 worldwide, #2 in the Middle East as of 2021),<sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">[238]</a></sup> University of Balamand (#501 worldwide as of 2021 <sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245">[239]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_American_University" title="Lebanese American University">Lebanese American University</a>(#551 worldwide as of 2021),<sup id="cite_ref-246" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-246">[240]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Universit%C3%A9_Saint_Joseph_de_Beyrouth" class="mw-redirect" title="Université Saint Joseph de Beyrouth">Université Saint Joseph de Beyrouth</a> (#541 worldwide as of 2021),<sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247">[241]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Universit%C3%A9_Libanaise" class="mw-redirect" title="Université Libanaise">Université Libanaise</a> (#3,826 worldwide) and <a href="/wiki/Holy_Spirit_University_of_Kaslik" title="Holy Spirit University of Kaslik">Holy Spirit University of Kaslik</a> (#600s worldwide as of 2020).<sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248">[242]</a></sup> Notre Dame University-Louaize NDU #701 as of 2021 <sup id="cite_ref-249" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-249">[243]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Lebanon" title="Health in Lebanon">Health in Lebanon</a>
      </div> 
      <p>In 2010, spending on healthcare accounted for 7.03% of the country's GDP. In 2009, there were 31.29 physicians and 19.71 nurses per 10,000 inhabitants.<sup id="cite_ref-250" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-250">[244]</a></sup> The life expectancy at birth was 72.59 years in 2011, or 70.48 years for males and 74.80 years for females.<sup id="cite_ref-251" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-251">[245]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>By the end of the civil war, only one-third of the country's public hospitals were operational, each with an average of only 20 beds. By 2009 the country had 28 public hospitals, with a total of 2,550 beds, while currently the country had an approximate of 25 public hospitals.<sup id="cite_ref-healthref_252-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-healthref-252">[246]</a></sup> At public hospitals, hospitalized uninsured patients pay 5% of the bill, in comparison with 15% in private hospitals, with the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://moph.gov.lb/en">Ministry of Public Health</a> reimbursing the remainder.<sup id="cite_ref-healthref_252-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-healthref-252">[246]</a></sup> The Ministry of Public Health contracts with 138 private hospitals and 25 public hospitals.<sup id="cite_ref-statbul11_253-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-statbul11-253">[247]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2011, there were 236,643 subsidized admissions to hospitals; 164,244 in private hospitals, and 72,399 in public hospitals. More patients visit private hospitals than public hospitals, because the private beds supply is higher.<sup id="cite_ref-statbul11_253-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-statbul11-253">[247]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>According to the Ministry of Public Health in Lebanon, the top 10 leading causes of reported hospital deaths in 2017 were: malignant neoplasm of bronchus or lung (4.6%), Acute <a href="/wiki/Myocardial_infarction" title="Myocardial infarction">myocardial infarction</a> (3%), <a href="/wiki/Pneumonia" title="Pneumonia">pneumonia</a> (2.2%), exposure to unspecified factor, unspecified place (2.1%), <a href="/wiki/Acute_kidney_injury" title="Acute kidney injury">acute kidney injury</a> (1.4%), intra-cerebral hemorrhage (1.2%), malignant neoplasm of colon (1.2%), malignant neoplasm of pancreas (1.1%), malignant neoplasm of prostate (1.1%), malignant neoplasm of bladder (0.8%).<sup id="cite_ref-254" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-254">[248]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Recently, there has been an increase in foodborne illnesses which has put an emphasis on the importance of the safety of the food chain in Lebanon. This raised the illues<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="&quot;illues&quot; does not appear to be an English word (August 2020)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> public awareness. More restaurants are seeking information and compliance with <a href="/wiki/International_Organization_for_Standardization" title="International Organization for Standardization">International Organization for Standardization</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-kebabs_255-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kebabs-255">[249]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Lebanon" title="Demographics of Lebanon">Demographics of Lebanon</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_people" title="Lebanese people">Lebanese people</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Beirutpic.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Beirutpic.jpg/220px-Beirutpic.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="142" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Beirutpic.jpg/330px-Beirutpic.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Beirutpic.jpg/440px-Beirutpic.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1251" data-file-height="810"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Beirutpic.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Beirut" title="Beirut">Beirut</a> located on the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">Mediterranean Sea</a> is the most populous city in Lebanon.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The population of Lebanon was estimated to be 6,859,408 in 2018, with the number of <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_people" title="Lebanese people">Lebanese nationals</a> estimated to be 4,680,212 (July 2018 est.);<sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-10">[6]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_2019_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP_2019-11">[7]</a></sup> however, no official census has been conducted since 1932 due to the sensitive <a href="/wiki/Confessionalism_(politics)" title="Confessionalism (politics)">confessional political balance</a> between Lebanon's various religious groups.<sup id="cite_ref-256" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-256">[250]</a></sup> Identifying all Lebanese as ethnically <a href="/wiki/Arab" class="mw-redirect" title="Arab">Arab</a> is a widely employed example of <a href="/wiki/Panethnicity" title="Panethnicity">panethnicity</a> since in reality, the Lebanese "are descended from many different peoples who are either indigenous, or have occupied, invaded, or settled this corner of the world", making Lebanon, "a mosaic of closely interrelated cultures".<sup id="cite_ref-Stokes,_Jamie_page_406_257-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stokes,_Jamie_page_406-257">[251]</a></sup> While at first glance, this ethnic, linguistic, religious and denominational diversity might seem to cause civil and political unrest, "for much of Lebanon’s history this multitudinous diversity of religious communities has coexisted with little conflict".<sup id="cite_ref-Stokes,_Jamie_page_406_257-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stokes,_Jamie_page_406-257">[251]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Fertility_rate" class="mw-redirect" title="Fertility rate">fertility rate</a> fell from 5.00 in 1971 to 1.75 in 2004. Fertility rates vary considerably among the different religious groups: in 2004, it was 2.10 for <a href="/wiki/Shia_Islam_in_Lebanon" class="mw-redirect" title="Shia Islam in Lebanon">Shiites</a>, 1.76 <a href="/wiki/Sunni_Islam_in_Lebanon" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunni Islam in Lebanon">Sunnis</a> and 1.61 for <a href="/wiki/Maronite_Christianity_in_Lebanon" class="mw-redirect" title="Maronite Christianity in Lebanon">Maronites</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-demo-reality_258-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-demo-reality-258">[252]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Lebanon has witnessed a series of migration waves: over 1,800,000 people emigrated from the country in the 1975–2011 period.<sup id="cite_ref-demo-reality_258-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-demo-reality-258">[252]</a></sup> Millions of <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_diaspora" title="Lebanese diaspora">people of Lebanese descent</a> are spread throughout the world, mostly Christians,<sup id="cite_ref-259" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-259">[253]</a></sup> especially in <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-260" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-260">[254]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_Brazilians" title="Lebanese Brazilians">Brazil</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_Argentines" title="Lebanese Argentines">Argentina</a> have large expatriate population.<sup id="cite_ref-261" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-261">[255]</a></sup> <i>(See <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_people" title="Lebanese people">Lebanese people</a>)</i>. Large numbers of Lebanese migrated to <a href="/wiki/West_Africa" title="West Africa">West Africa</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-262" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-262">[256]</a></sup> particularly to the <a href="/wiki/Ivory_Coast" title="Ivory Coast">Ivory Coast</a> (home to over 100,000 Lebanese)<sup id="cite_ref-263" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-263">[257]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Senegal" title="Senegal">Senegal</a> (roughly 30,000 <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_people_in_Senegal" title="Lebanese people in Senegal">Lebanese</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-264" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-264">[258]</a></sup> Australia is home to over 270,000 <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_Australian" class="mw-redirect" title="Lebanese Australian">Lebanese</a> (1999 est.).<sup id="cite_ref-265" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-265">[259]</a></sup> In Canada, there is also a large Lebanese diaspora of approximately 250,000–700,000 people having Lebanese descent. (see <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_Canadians" title="Lebanese Canadians">Lebanese Canadians</a>). Another region with a significant diaspora is the Persian Gulf, where the countries of Bahrain, Kuwait, Oman, Qatar (around 25,000 people),<sup id="cite_ref-266" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-266">[260]</a></sup> Saudi Arabia and UAE act as host countries to many Lebanese. </p>
      <p>As of 2012<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Lebanon&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Lebanon was host to over 1,600,000 <a href="/wiki/Refugee" title="Refugee">refugees</a> and <a href="/wiki/Right_of_asylum" title="Right of asylum">asylum</a> seekers: 449,957 from <a href="/wiki/Palestinians_in_Lebanon" title="Palestinians in Lebanon">Palestine</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-cia_15-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-15">[11]</a></sup> 8,000 from <a href="/wiki/Iraqis_in_Lebanon" title="Iraqis in Lebanon">Iraq</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-267" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-267">[261]</a></sup> over 1,100,000 from <a href="/wiki/Syrians_in_Lebanon" title="Syrians in Lebanon">Syria</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-cia_15-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-15">[11]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-268" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-268">[262]</a></sup> and 4,000 from <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudan</a>. According to the Economic and Social Commission for Western Asia of the United Nations, among the Syrian refugees, 71% live in poverty.<sup id="cite_ref-chronicle.fanack.com_220-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chronicle.fanack.com-220">[214]</a></sup> A 2013 estimate by the United Nations put the number of <a href="/wiki/Refugees_of_the_Syrian_civil_war" title="Refugees of the Syrian civil war">Syrian refugees</a> at more than 1,250,000.<sup id="cite_ref-refugees_114-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-refugees-114">[108]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the last three decades, lengthy and destructive <a href="/wiki/Armed_conflict" class="mw-redirect" title="Armed conflict">armed conflicts</a> have ravaged the country. The majority of Lebanese have been affected by armed conflict; those with direct personal experience include 75% of the population, and most others report suffering a range of hardships. In total, almost the entire population (96%) has been affected in some way – either personally or because of the wider consequences of armed conflict.<sup id="cite_ref-269" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-269">[263]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><br> </p>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Lebanon" title="Religion in Lebanon">Religion in Lebanon</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_Lebanon" title="Christianity in Lebanon">Christianity</a>, <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Lebanon" title="Islam in Lebanon">Islam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Irreligion_in_Lebanon" title="Irreligion in Lebanon">Irreligion</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Secularism_in_Lebanon" title="Secularism in Lebanon">Secularism in Lebanon</a>
      </div>

         <div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:0; top:0; border-width:0 200px 200px 0; border-color:SaddleBrown"></div>
         <div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 277.7606853915px; border-left-color:DodgerBlue"></div>

         <div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;right:100px; top:100px; border-width:24.868988716485px 96.858316112863px 0 0; border-top-color:MediumSeaGreen"></div>

        <div class="thumbcaption"> 
         <p>Religion in Lebanon (est. 2012)<sup id="cite_ref-cia.gov_270-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-270">[264]</a></sup> </p> 
         <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r981673959">.mw-parser-output .legend{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .legend-color{display:inline-block;min-width:1.25em;height:1.25em;line-height:1.25;margin:1px 0;text-align:center;border:1px solid black;background-color:transparent;color:black}.mw-parser-output .legend-text{}</style>
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:MediumSeaGreen; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Lebanon" title="Islam in Lebanon">Islam</a> (54%)
         </div>
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:DodgerBlue; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_Lebanon" title="Christianity in Lebanon">Christianity</a> (40.5%)
         </div>
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:SaddleBrown; color:white;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Lebanese_Druze" title="Lebanese Druze">Druze</a> (5.6%)
         </div> 
        </div> 
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Lebanon is the most religiously diverse country in the Middle East.<sup id="cite_ref-271" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-271">[265]</a></sup> As of 2014<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Lebanon&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/CIA_World_Factbook" class="mw-redirect" title="CIA World Factbook">CIA World Factbook</a> estimates the following: <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Lebanon" title="Islam in Lebanon">Muslim</a> 54% (27% <a href="/wiki/Sunni_Islam_in_Lebanon" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunni Islam in Lebanon">Sunni Islam</a>, 27% <a href="/wiki/Shia_Islam_in_Lebanon" class="mw-redirect" title="Shia Islam in Lebanon">Shia Islam</a>), <a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_Lebanon" title="Christianity in Lebanon">Christian</a> 40.5% (includes 21% <a href="/wiki/Maronite_Christianity_in_Lebanon" class="mw-redirect" title="Maronite Christianity in Lebanon">Maronite</a> Catholic, 8% <a href="/wiki/Greek_Orthodox_Christianity_in_Lebanon" class="mw-redirect" title="Greek Orthodox Christianity in Lebanon">Greek Orthodox</a>, 5% <a href="/wiki/Melkite_Christianity_in_Lebanon" class="mw-redirect" title="Melkite Christianity in Lebanon">Melkite</a> Catholic, 1% <a href="/wiki/Protestantism_in_Lebanon" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestantism in Lebanon">Protestant</a>, 5.5% other Christian), <a href="/wiki/Druze_in_Lebanon" class="mw-redirect" title="Druze in Lebanon">Druze</a> 5.6%, very small numbers of <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_Jews" class="mw-redirect" title="Lebanese Jews">Jews</a>, Baha'is, <a href="/wiki/Buddhist" class="mw-redirect" title="Buddhist">Buddhists</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hindu" class="mw-redirect" title="Hindu">Hindus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mormons" title="Mormons">Mormons</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cia.gov_270-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-270">[264]</a></sup> A study conducted by the Lebanese Information Center and based on voter registration numbers shows that by 2011 the Christian population was stable compared to that of previous years, making up 34.35% of the population; Muslims, the Druze included, were 65.47% of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-272" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-272">[266]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/World_Values_Survey" title="World Values Survey">World Values Survey</a> of 2014 put the percentage of <a href="/wiki/Atheism" title="Atheism">atheists</a> in Lebanon at 3.3%.<sup id="cite_ref-WVS_273-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WVS-273">[267]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:ChurchMosque.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/ChurchMosque.jpg/250px-ChurchMosque.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="236" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/ChurchMosque.jpg/375px-ChurchMosque.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/ChurchMosque.jpg/500px-ChurchMosque.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="965"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:ChurchMosque.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Saint_George_Maronite_Cathedral,_Beirut" class="mw-redirect" title="Saint George Maronite Cathedral, Beirut">Saint George Maronite Cathedral</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Mohammad_Al-Amin_Mosque" title="Mohammad Al-Amin Mosque">Mohammad Al-Amin Mosque</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beirut" title="Beirut">Beirut</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Lebanon_religious_groups_distribution.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Lebanon_religious_groups_distribution.jpg/170px-Lebanon_religious_groups_distribution.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="219" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Lebanon_religious_groups_distribution.jpg/255px-Lebanon_religious_groups_distribution.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Lebanon_religious_groups_distribution.jpg/340px-Lebanon_religious_groups_distribution.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2700" data-file-height="3484"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Lebanon_religious_groups_distribution.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Distribution of main religious groups of Lebanon according to last municipal election data.<sup id="cite_ref-274" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-274">[268]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Only_Time_Will_Tell.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Only_Time_Will_Tell.jpg/220px-Only_Time_Will_Tell.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Only_Time_Will_Tell.jpg/330px-Only_Time_Will_Tell.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Only_Time_Will_Tell.jpg/440px-Only_Time_Will_Tell.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1500" data-file-height="1000"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Only_Time_Will_Tell.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>In 1870, the first Evangelical Church was built in Beirut. During the Lebanese civil war (1975–1990) it was totally destroyed except for the bell tower. The church was rebuilt in 1998.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>It is believed that there has been a decline in the ratio of Christians to Muslims over the past 60 years, due to higher emigration rates of Christians, and a higher birth rate in the Muslim population.<sup id="cite_ref-freedom_275-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-freedom-275">[269]</a></sup> When the last census was held in 1932, Christians made up 53% of Lebanon's population.<sup id="cite_ref-demo-reality_258-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-demo-reality-258">[252]</a></sup> In 1956, it was estimated that the population was 54% Christian and 44% Muslim.<sup id="cite_ref-demo-reality_258-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-demo-reality-258">[252]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>A demographic study conducted by the research firm <a href="/w/index.php?title=Statistics_Lebanon&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Statistics Lebanon (page does not exist)">Statistics Lebanon</a> found that approximately 27% of the population was <a href="/wiki/Sunni_Islam_in_Lebanon" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunni Islam in Lebanon">Sunni</a>, 27% <a href="/wiki/Shia_Islam_in_Lebanon" class="mw-redirect" title="Shia Islam in Lebanon">Shia</a>, 21% <a href="/wiki/Maronite_Christianity_in_Lebanon" class="mw-redirect" title="Maronite Christianity in Lebanon">Maronite</a>, 8% <a href="/wiki/Greek_Orthodox_Christianity_in_Lebanon" class="mw-redirect" title="Greek Orthodox Christianity in Lebanon">Greek Orthodox</a>, 5% <a href="/wiki/Druze_in_Lebanon" class="mw-redirect" title="Druze in Lebanon">Druze</a>, 5% <a href="/wiki/Melkite_Christianity_in_Lebanon" class="mw-redirect" title="Melkite Christianity in Lebanon">Melkite</a>, and 1% <a href="/wiki/Protestantism_in_Lebanon" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestantism in Lebanon">Protestant</a>, with the remaining 6% mostly belonging to smaller non-native to Lebanon Christian denominations.<sup id="cite_ref-freedom_275-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-freedom-275">[269]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Other sources like <a href="/wiki/Euronews" title="Euronews">Euronews</a><sup id="cite_ref-276" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-276">[270]</a></sup> or the <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">Madrid-based</a> diary <i><a href="/wiki/La_Raz%C3%B3n_(Madrid)" title="La Razón (Madrid)">La Razón</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-277" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-277">[271]</a></sup> estimate the percentage of Christians to be around 53%. </p>
      <p>Because the relative size of confessional groups remains a sensitive issue, a national census has not been conducted since 1932.<sup id="cite_ref-freedom_275-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-freedom-275">[269]</a></sup> There are 18 state-recognized religious sects – four <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Lebanon" title="Islam in Lebanon">Muslim</a>, 12 <a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_Lebanon" title="Christianity in Lebanon">Christian</a>, one <a href="/wiki/Druze_in_Lebanon" class="mw-redirect" title="Druze in Lebanon">Druze</a>, and one <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_Jews" class="mw-redirect" title="Lebanese Jews">Jewish</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-freedom_275-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-freedom-275">[269]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Sunni_Islam_in_Lebanon" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunni Islam in Lebanon">Sunni residents</a> primarily live in Tripoli, Western Beirut, the Southern coast of Lebanon, and Northern Lebanon.<sup id="cite_ref-LOC_glossary_278-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LOC_glossary-278">[272]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Shia_Islam_in_Lebanon" class="mw-redirect" title="Shia Islam in Lebanon">Shi'a residents</a> primarily live in Southern Beirut, the <a href="/wiki/Beqaa_Valley" title="Beqaa Valley">Beqaa Valley</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Southern_Lebanon" title="Southern Lebanon">Southern Lebanon</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-LOC_glossary_278-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LOC_glossary-278">[272]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Maronite_Christianity_in_Lebanon" class="mw-redirect" title="Maronite Christianity in Lebanon">Maronite residents</a> primarily live in Eastern Beirut and the mountains of Lebanon.<sup id="cite_ref-LOC_glossary_278-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LOC_glossary-278">[272]</a></sup> They are the largest Christian community in Lebanon.<sup id="cite_ref-LOC_glossary_278-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LOC_glossary-278">[272]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Greek_Orthodox_Christianity_in_Lebanon" class="mw-redirect" title="Greek Orthodox Christianity in Lebanon">Greek Orthodox</a>, the second largest Christian community in Lebanon, primarily live in Koura, Beirut, Rachaya, Matn, Aley, Akkar, in the countryside around Tripoli, Hasbaya and Marjeyoun. They are a minority of 10% in Zahle.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>The Greek Catholics live mainly in Beirut, on the eastern slopes of the Lebanon mountains and in Zahle which is predominantly Greek Catholic.<sup id="cite_ref-279" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-279">[273]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the Christian village of Hadat, there has been a municipal ban on Muslims from buying or renting property. It has been claimed that it is due to an underlying fear of mixing with one another's salvation since for three decades, the village of Hadat has been predominantly Christian.<sup id="cite_ref-280" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-280">[274]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-281" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-281">[275]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Lebanese government tend to count its <a href="/wiki/Druze" title="Druze">Druze</a> citizens as part of its <a href="/wiki/Muslim" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslim">Muslim</a> population,<sup id="cite_ref-DruzeAreCountedAsMuslimsInLebanon_282-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DruzeAreCountedAsMuslimsInLebanon-282">[276]</a></sup> even though most <a href="/wiki/Druze" title="Druze">Druze</a> do not identify as <a href="/wiki/Muslims" title="Muslims">Muslims</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-283" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-283">[277]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-284" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-284">[278]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-285" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-285">[279]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-286" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-286">[280]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-287" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-287">[281]</a></sup> and they do not accept the <a href="/wiki/Five_Pillars_of_Islam" title="Five Pillars of Islam">five pillars of Islam</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-288" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-288">[282]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="***REMOVED***">Language</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_Arabic" title="Lebanese Arabic">Lebanese Arabic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Modern_Standard_Arabic" title="Modern Standard Arabic">Modern Standard Arabic</a>, and <a href="/wiki/French_language_in_Lebanon" title="French language in Lebanon">French language in Lebanon</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Article 11 of Lebanon's Constitution states that "Arabic is the official national language. A law determines the cases in which the <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French language</a> is to be used".<sup id="cite_ref-article_11_289-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-article_11-289">[283]</a></sup> The majority of Lebanese people speak <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_Arabic" title="Lebanese Arabic">Lebanese Arabic</a>, which is grouped in a larger category called <a href="/wiki/Levantine_Arabic" title="Levantine Arabic">Levantine Arabic</a>, while <a href="/wiki/Modern_Standard_Arabic" title="Modern Standard Arabic">Modern Standard Arabic</a> is mostly used in magazines, newspapers, and formal broadcast media. <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_Sign_Language" class="mw-redirect" title="Lebanese Sign Language">Lebanese Sign Language</a> is the language of the Deaf community. Almost 40% of Lebanese are considered <a href="/wiki/Francophone" class="mw-redirect" title="Francophone">francophone</a>, and another 15% "partial francophone", and 70% of Lebanon's secondary schools use French as a second language of instruction.<sup id="cite_ref-NadeauBarlow2008_290-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NadeauBarlow2008-290">[284]</a></sup> By comparison, English is used as a secondary language in 30% of Lebanon's secondary schools.<sup id="cite_ref-NadeauBarlow2008_290-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NadeauBarlow2008-290">[284]</a></sup> The use of French is a legacy of France's historic ties to the region, including its <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations_mandate" title="League of Nations mandate">League of Nations mandate</a> over Lebanon following World War I; as of 2005<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Lebanon&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, some 20% of the population used French on a daily basis.<sup id="cite_ref-Britannica2_291-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica2-291">[285]</a></sup> The use of Arabic by Lebanon's educated youth is declining, as they usually prefer to speak in French and, to a lesser extent, English, which are seen as more fashionable.<sup id="cite_ref-292" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-292">[286]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-293" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-293">[287]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>English is increasingly used in science and business interactions.<sup id="cite_ref-294" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-294">[288]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-295" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-295">[289]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_nationality_law" title="Lebanese nationality law">Lebanese citizens</a> of <a href="/wiki/Armenians_in_Lebanon" title="Armenians in Lebanon">Armenian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greeks_in_Lebanon" title="Greeks in Lebanon">Greek</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Assyrians_in_Lebanon" title="Assyrians in Lebanon">Assyrian</a> descent often speak their ancestral languages with varying degrees of fluency. As of 2009<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Lebanon&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, there were around 150,000 Armenians in Lebanon, or around 5% of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-296" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-296">[290]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Lebanon" title="Culture of Lebanon">Culture of Lebanon</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Baalbek-Bacchus.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Baalbek-Bacchus.jpg/220px-Baalbek-Bacchus.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Baalbek-Bacchus.jpg/330px-Baalbek-Bacchus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Baalbek-Bacchus.jpg/440px-Baalbek-Bacchus.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="600"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Baalbek-Bacchus.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Temple_of_Bacchus" title="Temple of Bacchus">Temple of Bacchus</a> is considered one of the best preserved <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman</a> temples in the world, c. 150 AD
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The culture of Lebanon reflects the legacy of various civilizations spanning thousands of years. Originally home to the <a href="/wiki/Canaan" title="Canaan">Canaanite</a>-<a href="/wiki/Phoenicia" title="Phoenicia">Phoenicians</a>, and then subsequently conquered and occupied by the <a href="/wiki/Assyria" title="Assyria">Assyrians</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Persia" class="mw-redirect" title="Persia">Persians</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Greeks" title="Greeks">Greeks</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Romans</a>, the Arabs, the <a href="/wiki/Fatimids" class="mw-redirect" title="Fatimids">Fatimids</a>, the Crusaders, the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Turks" title="Ottoman Turks">Ottoman Turks</a> and most recently the French, Lebanese culture has over the millennia evolved by borrowing from all of these groups. Lebanon's diverse population, composed of different ethnic and religious groups, has further contributed to the country's festivals, musical styles and literature as well as cuisine. Despite the ethnic, linguistic, religious and denominational diversity of the Lebanese, they "share an almost common culture".<sup id="cite_ref-StokesJamie_297-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-StokesJamie-297">[291]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_Arabic" title="Lebanese Arabic">Lebanese Arabic</a> is universally spoken while food, music, and literature are deep-rooted "in wider Mediterranean and Arab Levantine norms".<sup id="cite_ref-StokesJamie_297-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-StokesJamie-297">[291]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arts">Arts</span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Sursock_house.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Sursock_house.jpg/220px-Sursock_house.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Sursock_house.jpg/330px-Sursock_house.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Sursock_house.jpg/440px-Sursock_house.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2048"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Sursock_house.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Sursock_Museum" title="Sursock Museum">Sursock Museum</a> in Beirut
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:127px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Votive_statue_from_eshmun.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Beige marble statue of a stout young child aged about two years old lying on his left side. The child's head is shaved, his eyes gaze over the viewer's shoulder and his lower body is covered in a draping cloth that hangs limply between his flexed feet. The child supports his torso with his left hand in which he holds an unidentifiable object, he also holds a small bird in his right hand. The sculpture rests on a heavy socle inscribed with barely visible letters spanning the upper part of the socle vertically." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Votive_statue_from_eshmun.jpg/125px-Votive_statue_from_eshmun.jpg" decoding="async" width="125" height="94" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Votive_statue_from_eshmun.jpg/188px-Votive_statue_from_eshmun.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Votive_statue_from_eshmun.jpg/250px-Votive_statue_from_eshmun.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2378" data-file-height="1788"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Votive_statue_from_eshmun.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Votive marble statue of a royal child, inscribed in Phoenician from the <a href="/wiki/Eshmun" title="Eshmun">Eshmun</a> sanctuary, c. 400s BC
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In visual arts, <a href="/wiki/Moustafa_Farroukh" title="Moustafa Farroukh">Moustafa Farroukh</a> was one of Lebanon's most prominent painters of the 20th century. Formally trained in Rome and Paris, he exhibited in venues from Paris to New York to Beirut over his career.<sup id="cite_ref-298" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-298">[292]</a></sup> Many more contemporary artists are currently active, such as <a href="/wiki/Walid_Raad" title="Walid Raad">Walid Raad</a>, a contemporary media artist currently residing in New York.<sup id="cite_ref-299" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-299">[293]</a></sup> In the field of photography, the <a href="/wiki/Arab_Image_Foundation" title="Arab Image Foundation">Arab Image Foundation</a> has a collection of over 400,000 photographs from Lebanon and the Middle East. The photographs can be viewed in a research center and various events and publications have been produced in Lebanon and worldwide to promote the collection. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span></h3> 
      <p>In literature, <a href="/wiki/Khalil_Gibran" class="mw-redirect" title="Khalil Gibran">Khalil Gibran</a> is the third best-selling poet of all time, behind <a href="/wiki/William_Shakespeare" title="William Shakespeare">Shakespeare</a> and <a href="/wiki/Laozi" title="Laozi">Laozi</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-300" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-300">[294]</a></sup> He is particularly known for his book <i><a href="/wiki/The_Prophet_(book)" title="The Prophet (book)">The Prophet</a></i> (1923), which has been translated into more than twenty different languages and is the second best selling book in the 20th century behind <a href="/wiki/The_Bible" class="mw-redirect" title="The Bible">the Bible</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-301" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-301">[295]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Ameen_Rihani" title="Ameen Rihani">Ameen Rihani</a> was a major figure in the mahjar literary movement developed by Arab emigrants in North America, and an early theorist of <a href="/wiki/Arab_nationalism" title="Arab nationalism">Arab nationalism</a>. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Mikha%27il_Na%27ima" class="mw-redirect" title="Mikha'il Na'ima">Mikha'il Na'ima</a> is widely recognized as one of the most important figures in modern Arabic letters and one of the most important spiritual writers of the 20th century. </p>
      <p>Several contemporary Lebanese writers have also achieved international success; including <a href="/wiki/Elias_Khoury" title="Elias Khoury">Elias Khoury</a>, <a href="/wiki/Amin_Maalouf" title="Amin Maalouf">Amin Maalouf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hanan_al-Shaykh" title="Hanan al-Shaykh">Hanan al-Shaykh</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Georges_Schehad%C3%A9" title="Georges Schehadé">Georges Schehadé</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Lebanon" title="Music of Lebanon">Music of Lebanon</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:127px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Fairuz_in_btd_concert_2001.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Fairuz_in_btd_concert_2001.jpg/125px-Fairuz_in_btd_concert_2001.jpg" decoding="async" width="125" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Fairuz_in_btd_concert_2001.jpg/188px-Fairuz_in_btd_concert_2001.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Fairuz_in_btd_concert_2001.jpg/250px-Fairuz_in_btd_concert_2001.jpg 2x" data-file-width="564" data-file-height="753"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Fairuz_in_btd_concert_2001.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Fairuz" title="Fairuz">Fairuz</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>While traditional folk music remains popular in Lebanon, modern music reconciling Western and traditional Arabic styles, pop, and <a href="/wiki/Fusion_(music)" class="mw-redirect" title="Fusion (music)">fusion</a> are rapidly advancing in popularity.<sup id="cite_ref-Traditional_302-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Traditional-302">[296]</a></sup> Lebanese artists like <a href="/wiki/Fairuz" title="Fairuz">Fairuz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wadih_El_Safi" title="Wadih El Safi">Wadih El Safi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sabah" title="Sabah">Sabah</a>, <a href="/wiki/Julia_Boutros" title="Julia Boutros">Julia Boutros</a> or <a href="/wiki/Najwa_Karam" title="Najwa Karam">Najwa Karam</a> are widely known and appreciated in Lebanon and in the Arab world. Radio stations feature a variety of music, including traditional Lebanese, classical Arabic, Armenian<sup id="cite_ref-303" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-303">[297]</a></sup> and modern French, English, American, and <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin</a> tunes.<sup id="cite_ref-304" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-304">[298]</a></sup> </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Courtyard_at_Beiteddine_Palace_-_2009.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Courtyard_at_Beiteddine_Palace_-_2009.jpg/220px-Courtyard_at_Beiteddine_Palace_-_2009.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Courtyard_at_Beiteddine_Palace_-_2009.jpg/330px-Courtyard_at_Beiteddine_Palace_-_2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Courtyard_at_Beiteddine_Palace_-_2009.jpg/440px-Courtyard_at_Beiteddine_Palace_-_2009.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3880" data-file-height="2608"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Courtyard_at_Beiteddine_Palace_-_2009.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Beiteddine_Palace" title="Beiteddine Palace">Beiteddine Palace</a>, venue of the <a href="/wiki/Beiteddine_Festival" title="Beiteddine Festival">Beiteddine Festival</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media_and_cinema">Media and cinema</span></h3> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Lebanon" title="Cinema of Lebanon">cinema of Lebanon</a>, according to film critic and historian, Roy Armes, was the only cinema in the Arabic-speaking region, other than Egypt's, that could amount to a national cinema.<sup id="cite_ref-305" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-305">[299]</a></sup> Cinema in Lebanon has been in existence since the 1920s, and the country has produced over 500 films.<sup id="cite_ref-306" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-306">[300]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Media_of_Lebanon" class="mw-redirect" title="Media of Lebanon">media of Lebanon</a> is not only a regional center of production but also the most liberal and free in the Arab world.<sup id="cite_ref-307" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-307">[301]</a></sup> According to Press freedom's <a href="/wiki/Reporters_Without_Borders" title="Reporters Without Borders">Reporters Without Borders</a>, "the media have more freedom in Lebanon than in any other Arab country".<sup id="cite_ref-308" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-308">[302]</a></sup> Despite its small population and geographic size, Lebanon plays an influential role in the production of information in the Arab world and is "at the core of a regional media network with global implications".<sup id="cite_ref-b1_309-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-b1-309">[303]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Holidays_and_festivals">Holidays and festivals</span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Centre-ville_de_Beyrouth.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Centre-ville_de_Beyrouth.JPG/220px-Centre-ville_de_Beyrouth.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Centre-ville_de_Beyrouth.JPG/330px-Centre-ville_de_Beyrouth.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Centre-ville_de_Beyrouth.JPG/440px-Centre-ville_de_Beyrouth.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2816" data-file-height="2112"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Centre-ville_de_Beyrouth.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Roman baths park in Downtown <a href="/wiki/Beirut" title="Beirut">Beirut</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_Lebanon" title="Public holidays in Lebanon">Public holidays in Lebanon</a>
      </div>
      <p>Lebanon celebrates national and both <a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_Lebanon" title="Christianity in Lebanon">Christian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Lebanon" title="Islam in Lebanon">Muslim</a> holidays. Christian holidays are celebrated following both the <a href="/wiki/Gregorian_Calendar" class="mw-redirect" title="Gregorian Calendar">Gregorian Calendar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Julian_Calendar" class="mw-redirect" title="Julian Calendar">Julian Calendar</a>. <a href="/wiki/Greek_Orthodox_Christianity_in_Lebanon" class="mw-redirect" title="Greek Orthodox Christianity in Lebanon">Greek Orthodox</a> (with the exception of Easter), <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism_in_Lebanon" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholicism in Lebanon">Catholics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Protestantism_in_Lebanon" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestantism in Lebanon">Protestants</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Melkite_Christianity_in_Lebanon" class="mw-redirect" title="Melkite Christianity in Lebanon">Melkite</a> Christians follow the Gregorian Calendar and thus celebrate Christmas on 25 December. Armenian <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Apostolic_Church" title="Armenian Apostolic Church">Apostolic</a> Christians celebrate Christmas on 6 January, as they follow the Julian Calendar. Muslim holidays are followed based on the Islamic lunar calendar. Muslim holidays that are celebrated include Eid al-Fitr (the three-day feast at the end of the Ramadan month), Eid al-Adha (The Feast of the Sacrifice) which is celebrated during the annual pilgrimage to Mecca and also celebrates Abraham's willingness to sacrifice his son to God, the Birth of the Prophet Muhammad, and Ashura (the Shiite Day of Mourning). Lebanon's National Holidays include Workers Day, Independence day, and Martyrs Day. Music festivals, often hosted at historical sites, are a customary element of Lebanese culture.<sup id="cite_ref-Festivals_310-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Festivals-310">[304]</a></sup> Among the most famous are <a href="/wiki/Baalbeck_International_Festival" title="Baalbeck International Festival">Baalbeck International Festival</a>, <a href="/wiki/Byblos_International_Festival" title="Byblos International Festival">Byblos International Festival</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beiteddine_Festival" title="Beiteddine Festival">Beiteddine International Festival</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.jouniehinternationalfestival.com/">Jounieh International Festival</a>, Broumana Festival, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.batrounfestival.org/">Batroun International Festival</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.facebook.com/ehmejfestival/">Ehmej Festival</a>, Dhour Chwer Festival and Tyr Festival.<sup id="cite_ref-Festivals_310-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Festivals-310">[304]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-311" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-311">[305]</a></sup> These festivals are promoted by Lebanon's <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Tourism_(Lebanon)" title="Ministry of Tourism (Lebanon)">Ministry of Tourism</a>. Lebanon hosts about 15 concerts from international performers each year, ranking 1st for nightlife in the Middle East, and 6th worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-312" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-312">[306]</a></sup> </p>
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_cuisine" title="Lebanese cuisine">Lebanese cuisine</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Lebanese cuisine is similar to those of many countries in the Eastern Mediterranean, such as Syria, Turkey, Greece, and Cyprus. The Lebanese national dishes are the <a href="/wiki/Kibbe" class="mw-redirect" title="Kibbe">kibbe</a>, a meat pie made from finely minced <a href="/wiki/Lamb_and_mutton" title="Lamb and mutton">lamb</a> and <a href="/wiki/Burghul" class="mw-redirect" title="Burghul">burghul</a> (cracked <a href="/wiki/Wheat" title="Wheat">wheat</a>), and the <a href="/wiki/Tabbouleh" title="Tabbouleh">tabbouleh</a>, a salad made from <a href="/wiki/Parsley" title="Parsley">parsley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tomato" title="Tomato">tomatoes</a>, and burghul. The national beverage is <a href="/wiki/Arak_(drink)" title="Arak (drink)">arak</a>, a strong <a href="/wiki/Anise" title="Anise">anise</a>-flavored liquor made from fermented <a href="/wiki/Grape_juice" title="Grape juice">grape juice</a>. It is usually drunk with water and ice, which turns the clear liquid milky-white, and usually accompanies food. Arak is a strong spirit similar to the Greek ouzo and the Turkish raki. Lebanese restaurant meals begin with a wide array of <a href="/wiki/Mezze" class="mw-redirect" title="Mezze">mezze</a> - small savoury dishes, such as dips, salads, and pastries. The mezze are typically followed by a selection of grilled <a href="/wiki/Meat" title="Meat">meat</a> or <a href="/wiki/Fish" title="Fish">fish</a>. In general, meals are finished with <a href="/wiki/Arabic_coffee" title="Arabic coffee">Arabic coffee</a> and fresh <a href="/wiki/Fruit" title="Fruit">fruit</a>, though sometimes a selection of traditional sweets will be offered as well. <a href="/wiki/M%27Juhdara" class="mw-redirect" title="M'Juhdara">M'Juhdara</a>, a thick stew of <a href="/wiki/Onions" class="mw-redirect" title="Onions">onions</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rice" title="Rice">rice</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Lentils" class="mw-redirect" title="Lentils">lentils</a>, is sometimes considered poor man's fare and is often eaten around <a href="/wiki/Lent" title="Lent">Lent</a> by people in the Lebanese diaspora. Beirut and its environs contain many restaurants of various national origins. At the same time, <a href="/wiki/Wine" title="Wine">wine</a> is growing in popularity and a number of vineyards currently exist in the <a href="/wiki/Bekaa_valley" class="mw-redirect" title="Bekaa valley">Bekaa valley</a> and elsewhere. <a href="/wiki/Beer" title="Beer">Beer</a> is also highly popular and Lebanon produces a number of local beers, of which <a href="/wiki/Almaza" class="mw-redirect" title="Almaza">almaza</a> is perhaps the most popular. </p> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{display:flex;flex-direction:row;clear:left;flex-wrap:wrap;width:100%;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{margin:1px;float:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:none!important;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle .thumbcaption{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow>.thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style>
      <div class="thumb tmulti tnone center" style="background-color:white">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:892px;max-width:892px;background-color:white">

         </div>

         </div>
