       </div>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Lebanon" title="Sport in Lebanon">Sport in Lebanon</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Camille_Chamoun_Sports_City_Stadium_2018_-_Beirut_derby_(Nejmeh_fans).png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Camille_Chamoun_Sports_City_Stadium_2018_-_Beirut_derby_%28Nejmeh_fans%29.png/220px-Camille_Chamoun_Sports_City_Stadium_2018_-_Beirut_derby_%28Nejmeh_fans%29.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="113" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Camille_Chamoun_Sports_City_Stadium_2018_-_Beirut_derby_%28Nejmeh_fans%29.png/330px-Camille_Chamoun_Sports_City_Stadium_2018_-_Beirut_derby_%28Nejmeh_fans%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Camille_Chamoun_Sports_City_Stadium_2018_-_Beirut_derby_%28Nejmeh_fans%29.png/440px-Camille_Chamoun_Sports_City_Stadium_2018_-_Beirut_derby_%28Nejmeh_fans%29.png 2x" data-file-width="1440" data-file-height="739"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Camille_Chamoun_Sports_City_Stadium_2018_-_Beirut_derby_(Nejmeh_fans).png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Camille_Chamoun_Sports_City_Stadium" title="Camille Chamoun Sports City Stadium">Camille Chamoun Sports City Stadium</a> in <a href="/wiki/Beirut" title="Beirut">Beirut</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:2020-21_Ahed_vs_Ansar_02.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/2020-21_Ahed_vs_Ansar_02.jpg/220px-2020-21_Ahed_vs_Ansar_02.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/2020-21_Ahed_vs_Ansar_02.jpg/330px-2020-21_Ahed_vs_Ansar_02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/2020-21_Ahed_vs_Ansar_02.jpg/440px-2020-21_Ahed_vs_Ansar_02.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6000" data-file-height="4000"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:2020-21_Ahed_vs_Ansar_02.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Al_Ansar_FC" title="Al Ansar FC">Al Ansar FC</a> in <a href="/wiki/Beirut" title="Beirut">Beirut</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Lebanon has six <a href="/wiki/Skiing_in_Lebanon" title="Skiing in Lebanon">ski resorts</a>. Because of Lebanon's unique geography, it is possible to go skiing in the morning and swimming in the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">Mediterranean Sea</a> in the afternoon.<sup id="cite_ref-Aikman2009_313-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Aikman2009-313">[307]</a></sup> At the competitive level, basketball and <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> are among Lebanon's most popular sports. <a href="/wiki/Canoeing" title="Canoeing">Canoeing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cycling" title="Cycling">cycling</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rafting" title="Rafting">rafting</a>, <a href="/wiki/Climbing" title="Climbing">climbing</a>, swimming, sailing and <a href="/wiki/Caving" title="Caving">caving</a> are among the other common leisure sports in Lebanon. The <a href="/wiki/Beirut_Marathon" title="Beirut Marathon">Beirut Marathon</a> is held every fall, drawing top runners from Lebanon and abroad.<sup id="cite_ref-314" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-314">[308]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Rugby_league_in_Lebanon" title="Rugby league in Lebanon">Rugby league</a> is a relatively new but growing sport in Lebanon. The <a href="/wiki/Lebanon_national_rugby_league_team" title="Lebanon national rugby league team">Lebanon national rugby league team</a> participated in the <a href="/wiki/2000_Rugby_League_World_Cup" title="2000 Rugby League World Cup">2000 Rugby League World Cup</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-315" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-315">[309]</a></sup> and narrowly missed qualification for the <a href="/wiki/2008_Rugby_League_World_Cup" title="2008 Rugby League World Cup">2008</a><sup id="cite_ref-316" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-316">[310]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/2013_Rugby_League_World_Cup" title="2013 Rugby League World Cup">2013</a> tournaments.<sup id="cite_ref-317" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-317">[311]</a></sup> Lebanon also took part in the <a href="/wiki/2009_European_Cup" title="2009 European Cup">2009 European Cup</a> where, after narrowly failing to qualify for the final, the team defeated <a href="/wiki/Ireland_national_rugby_league_team" title="Ireland national rugby league team">Ireland</a> to finish 3rd in the tournament.<sup id="cite_ref-318" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-318">[312]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hazem_El_Masri" title="Hazem El Masri">Hazem El Masri</a>, who was born in Tripoli, is considered to be the greatest <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_people" title="Lebanese people">Lebanese</a> to ever play the game. He immigrated to <a href="/wiki/Sydney" title="Sydney">Sydney</a>, Australia from Lebanon in 1988. He became the greatest point-scorer in <a href="/wiki/National_Rugby_League" title="National Rugby League">National Rugby League</a> history in 2009 by scoring himself 2418 points while playing for Australian club, <a href="/wiki/Canterbury-Bankstown_Bulldogs" title="Canterbury-Bankstown Bulldogs">Canterbury-Bankstown Bulldogs</a> where he also holds the record for most first grade appearances for the club with 317 games and most tries for the club with 159 tries. At international level, He also hold the records as top-try scorer with 12 tries and top-point scorer with 136 points for the Lebanese national team.<sup id="cite_ref-319" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-319">[313]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Lebanon participates in <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Lebanon_national_basketball_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Lebanon national basketball team">Lebanese National Team</a> qualified for the <a href="/wiki/FIBA_World_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="FIBA World Championship">FIBA World Championship</a> 3 times in a row.<sup id="cite_ref-320" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-320">[314]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-321" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-321">[315]</a></sup> Dominant basketball teams in Lebanon are <a href="/wiki/Sporting_Al_Riyadi_Beirut" class="mw-redirect" title="Sporting Al Riyadi Beirut">Sporting Al Riyadi Beirut</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-322" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-322">[316]</a></sup> who are the current Arab and Asian champions, <a href="/wiki/Hekmeh" class="mw-redirect" title="Hekmeh">Club Sagesse</a> who were able to earn the Asian and Arab championships before. <a href="/wiki/Fadi_El_Khatib" title="Fadi El Khatib">Fadi El Khatib</a> is the most decorated player in the Lebanese National Basketball League. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Football_in_Lebanon" title="Football in Lebanon">Football</a> is also one of the more popular sports in the country with the <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_Premier_League" title="Lebanese Premier League">Lebanese Premier League</a>, whose most successful clubs are the <a href="/wiki/Al-Ansar_Club" class="mw-redirect" title="Al-Ansar Club">Al-Ansar Club</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Nejmeh_SC" title="Nejmeh SC">Nejmeh SC</a>, with notable players being <a href="/wiki/Roda_Antar" title="Roda Antar">Roda Antar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Youssef_Mohamad" title="Youssef Mohamad">Youssef Mohamad</a>, the first Arab to captain a European premier league team. </p>
      <p>In recent years, Lebanon has hosted the <a href="/wiki/AFC_Asian_Cup" title="AFC Asian Cup">AFC Asian Cup</a><sup id="cite_ref-323" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-323">[317]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Pan_Arab_Games" title="Pan Arab Games">Pan Arab Games</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-324" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-324">[318]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-325" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-325">[319]</a></sup> Lebanon hosted the <a href="/wiki/2009_Jeux_de_la_Francophonie" title="2009 Jeux de la Francophonie">2009 Jeux de la Francophonie</a><sup id="cite_ref-326" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-326">[320]</a></sup> from 27 September to 6 October, and <a href="/wiki/Lebanon_at_the_Olympics" title="Lebanon at the Olympics">have participated</a> in every <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Games" title="Olympic Games">Olympic Games</a> since its independence, winning a total of four medals.<sup id="cite_ref-327" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-327">[321]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Prominent Lebanese bodybuilders include <a href="/wiki/Samir_Bannout" title="Samir Bannout">Samir Bannout</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mohammad_Bannout" title="Mohammad Bannout">Mohammad Bannout</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ahmad_Haidar" title="Ahmad Haidar">Ahmad Haidar</a>. </p>
      <p>Water sports have also shown to be very active in the past years, in Lebanon. Since 2012 and with the emergence of the Lebanon Water Festival NGO, more emphasis has been placed on those sports, and Lebanon has been pushed forward as a water sport destination internationally.<sup id="cite_ref-328" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-328">[322]</a></sup> They host different contests and water show sports that encourage their fans to participate and win big.<sup id="cite_ref-329" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-329">[323]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Science_and_technology">Science and technology</span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:USJ_Campus.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/USJ_Campus.jpg/220px-USJ_Campus.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="115" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/USJ_Campus.jpg/330px-USJ_Campus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/USJ_Campus.jpg/440px-USJ_Campus.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1281" data-file-height="668"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:USJ_Campus.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Campus of Innovation and Sports, Damascus Street, <a href="/wiki/Beirut" title="Beirut">Beirut</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Lebanon is a source for scientists, many known scientists had come from Lebanon like <a href="/wiki/Hassan_Kamel_Al-Sabbah" title="Hassan Kamel Al-Sabbah">Hassan Kamel Al-Sabbah</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rammal_Rammal" title="Rammal Rammal">Rammal Rammal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Edgar_Choueiri" title="Edgar Choueiri">Edgar Choueiri</a>...<sup id="cite_ref-330" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-330">[324]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-331" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-331">[325]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-332" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-332">[326]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1960, a science club from a university in Beirut started with a Lebanese space program, thus "<a href="/wiki/The_Lebanese_Rocket_Society" class="mw-redirect" title="The Lebanese Rocket Society">the Lebanese Rocket Society</a>" was emerged. They achieved great success until 1966 where the program was stopped because of both war and external pressure.<sup id="cite_ref-333" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-333">[327]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-334" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-334">[328]</a></sup> </p>

      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1011085734">.mw-parser-output .reflist{font-size:90%;margin-bottom:0.5em;list-style-type:decimal}.mw-parser-output .reflist .references{font-size:100%;margin-bottom:0;list-style-type:inherit}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-2{column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-3{column-width:25em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns{margin-top:0.3em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns ol{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns li{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-alpha{list-style-type:upper-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-roman{list-style-type:upper-roman}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-alpha{list-style-type:lower-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-greek{list-style-type:lower-greek}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-roman{list-style-type:lower-roman}</style>
      <div class="reflist reflist-lower-alpha"> 
       <div class="mw-references-wrap">
        <ol class="references"> 
         <li id="cite_note-17"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-17">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><i>Republic of Lebanon</i> is the most common phrase used by Lebanese government agencies. The phrase <i>Lebanese Republic</i> is a literal translation of the official <a href="/wiki/Arabic" title="Arabic">Arabic</a> and <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a> names, no longer in use.</span> </li> 
        </ol>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1011085734">
      <div class="reflist"> 
       <div class="mw-references-wrap">
        <ol class="references"> 
         <li id="cite_note-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Article 11 of the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Lebanon" title="Constitution of Lebanon">Constitution of Lebanon</a> states: "Arabic is the official national language. A law shall determine the cases in which the French language can be used." See: <a href="/wiki/French_language_in_Lebanon" title="French language in Lebanon">French language in Lebanon</a></span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-2"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-2">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Also simply called either Lebanese or Arabic, it is the daily spoken language of the vast majority of the local population. It also has a romanized written form used in informal communications.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-3"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-3">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"> Note: many Christian Lebanese do not identify themselves as Arab but rather as descendants of the ancient Canaanites and prefer to be called Phoenicians.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-4"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-4">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"> Lebanon encompasses a great mix of cultures and ethnic groups which have been building up for more than 6000 years. Most of the Lebanese are descendants of the Phoenicians/Canaanites and/or West Aramaic (50-70%). The second largest ethnic group in Lebanon descends from Arabs (20-30%). Armenians, Greeks, Assyrians, Hebrews, Kurds, Persians and others form about (10-20%).</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-90"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-90">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">2005: <a href="/wiki/Bassel_Fleihan" title="Bassel Fleihan">Bassel Fleihan</a>, Lebanese legislator and Minister of Economy and Commerce; <a href="/wiki/Samir_Kassir" title="Samir Kassir">Samir Kassir</a>, Columnist and <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Left_Movement_(Lebanon)" title="Democratic Left Movement (Lebanon)">Democratic Left Movement</a> leader; <a href="/wiki/George_Hawi" title="George Hawi">George Hawi</a>, former head of <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_Communist_Party" title="Lebanese Communist Party">Lebanese Communist Party</a>; <a href="/wiki/Gibran_Tueni" class="mw-redirect" title="Gibran Tueni">Gibran Tueni</a>, Editor in Chief of "An Nahar" newspaper. 2006: <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Gemayel" title="Pierre Gemayel">Pierre Gemayel</a>, Minister of Industry. 2007: <a href="/wiki/Walid_Eido" title="Walid Eido">Walid Eido</a>, MP; <a href="/wiki/Antoine_Ghanim" class="mw-redirect" title="Antoine Ghanim">Antoine Ghanim</a>, MP.</span> </li> 
        </ol>

          <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><cite id="CITEREFFirro,_Kais2003" class="citation book cs1">Firro, Kais (8 February 2003). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=zRwOcE9wJAQC&amp;pg=PA18"><i>Inventing Lebanon: Nationalism and the State Under the Mandate</i></a>. I.B.Tauris. p.&nbsp;18. <a href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-1-86064-857-1" title="Special:BookSources/978-1-86064-857-1"><bdi>978-1-86064-857-1</bdi></a>. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20130621074704/http://books.google.com/books?id=zRwOcE9wJAQC&amp;pg=PA18">Archived</a> from the original on 21 June 2013<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">2 April</span> 2013</span>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Inventing+Lebanon%3A+Nationalism+and+the+State+Under+the+Mandate&amp;rft.pages=18&amp;rft.pub=I.B.Tauris&amp;rft.date=2003-02-08&amp;rft.isbn=978-1-86064-857-1&amp;rft.au=Firro%2C+Kais&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DzRwOcE9wJAQC%26pg%3DPA18&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ALebanon" class="Z3988"></span></span> </li> 
        <li id="cite_note-Rooke-46"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Rooke_46-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">
          <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><cite id="CITEREFTetz_Rooke2013" class="citation book cs1">Tetz Rooke (2013). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=ykTYAQAAQBAJ&amp;pg=PA178">"Writing the Boundary: "Khitat al-Shăm" by Muhammad Kurd ʹAli"</a>. In Hiroyuki (ed.). <i>Concept Of Territory In Islamic Thought</i>. Routledge. p.&nbsp;178. <a href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-1-136-18453-6" title="Special:BookSources/978-1-136-18453-6"><bdi>978-1-136-18453-6</bdi></a>. <q>His [(<a href="/wiki/Thongchai_Winichakul" title="Thongchai Winichakul">Thongchai Winichakul</a>’s)] study shows that the modern map in some cases predicted the nation instead of just recording it; rather than describing existing borders it created the reality it was assumed to depict. The power of the map over the mind was great:"[H]ow could a nation resist being found if a nineteenth-century map had predicted it?" In the Middle East, Lebanon seems to offer a corresponding example. When the idea of a Greater Lebanon in 1908 was put forward in a book by Bulus Nujaym, a Lebanese Maronite writing under the pseudonym of M. Jouplain, he suggested that the natural boundaries of Lebanon were exactly the same as drawn in the 1861 and 1863 staff maps of the French military expedition to Syria, maps that added territories on the northern, eastern and southern borders, plus the city of Beirut, to the Mutasarrifiyya of Mount Lebanon. In this case, too, the prior existence of a European military map seems to have created a fact on the ground.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.atitle=Writing+the+Boundary%3A+%22Khitat+al-Sh%C4%83m%22+by+Muhammad+Kurd+%CA%B9Ali&amp;rft.btitle=Concept+Of+Territory+In+Islamic+Thought&amp;rft.pages=178&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.date=2013&amp;rft.isbn=978-1-136-18453-6&amp;rft.au=Tetz+Rooke&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DykTYAQAAQBAJ%26pg%3DPA178&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ALebanon" class="Z3988"></span></span> </li>
